However, modern neuroscience suggests that language processing isn't just localized to one area. There's evidence that multiple brain regions are involved in different aspects of language, such as comprehension, production, and processing. Okay, let's tackle this question. The user is John Smith, an accountant who avoids eggs because he thinks they raise cholesterol. The question is about which statement about eggs and cholesterol is true: A says eggs raise cholesterol levels, B says dietary cholesterol has little effect on blood cholesterol.

First, I need to recall what I know about eggs and cholesterol. Eggs are a common source of dietary cholesterol. But I remember that the relationship between dietary cholesterol and blood cholesterol isn't straightforward. The body produces most of the cholesterol we have, and dietary cholesterol from food like eggs might not have as big an effect as people used to think. 

I think the American Heart Association and other health organizations have updated their guidelines.
